    display: inline;

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

VULNERABILITY DETAILS



<b class="line"><!---->VULNERABILITY DETAILS<!----></b>



<br>





There seems to be a Unicode parsing vulnerability when a downloaded filename ends with carefully crafted Unicode characters.  Causes Chrome to repeatably crash. Specifically, the characters "П÷┴≤" at the end of a *long* file name crash chrome. 



<span class="line"><!---->There seems to be a Unicode parsing vulnerability when a downloaded filename ends with carefully crafted Unicode characters.  Causes Chrome to repeatably crash. Specifically, the characters "П÷┴≤" at the end of a *long* file name crash chrome. <!----></span>



<br>



<br>





VERSION



<b class="line"><!---->VERSION<!----></b>



<br>





Chrome Version: 105.0.5195.125 (Official Build) (64-bit)



<span class="line"><!---->Chrome Version: 105.0.5195.125 (Official Build) (64-bit)<!----></span>



<br>





Operating System: Linux Mint 20



<span class="line"><!---->Operating System: Linux Mint 20<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





REPRODUCTION CASE



<b class="line"><!---->REPRODUCTION CASE<!----></b>



<br>





Download a file that ends in specially crafted unicode characters



<span class="line"><!---->Download a file that ends in specially crafted unicode characters<!----></span>



<br>





Example file name: aaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaabbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbП÷┴≤.pdf



<span class="line"><!---->Example file name: aaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaabbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbbП÷┴≤.pdf<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





FOR CRASHES, PLEASE INCLUDE THE FOLLOWING ADDITIONAL INFORMATION



<b class="line"><!---->FOR CRASHES, PLEASE INCLUDE THE FOLLOWING ADDITIONAL INFORMATION<!----></b>

Hello, I did some more digging with the chrome://net-export running during a crash. I was able to create a completely reproducible crash running this simple python server.  It seems there is a problem with the  HTTP "Content-Disposition" header handling the strange filename.  I added the python script as an attachment.



<span class="line"><!---->Hello, I did some more digging with the chrome://net-export running during a crash. I was able to create a completely reproducible crash running this simple python server.  It seems there is a problem with the  HTTP "Content-Disposition" header handling the strange filename.  I added the python script as an attachment.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Can I request the URL in the script does not become public?

I think (although I didn't verify the cause of the assertion failure in the dbus code since I didn't have debugging symbols for it) that it looks like the problem here is that SelectFileDialog::GetShortenedFilePath is truncating the filename (where it does "file_string.resize(kMaxNameLength - extension.length());") in the middle of a UTF-8 sequence (in particular, after the first byte of a 3-byte sequence).  (It then appends more characters to the string.)



<span class="line"><!---->I think (although I didn't verify the cause of the assertion failure in the dbus code since I didn't have debugging symbols for it) that it looks like the problem here is that SelectFileDialog::GetShortenedFilePath is truncating the filename (where it does "file_string.resize(kMaxNameLength - extension.length());") in the middle of a UTF-8 sequence (in particular, after the first byte of a 3-byte sequence).  (It then appends more characters to the string.)<!----></span>

I reviewed the code you pointed out, this could potentially allow an attacker to craft a "content-disposition" header that would save a file in a location other than the user intended. For example, it allows a 12 char "final extension". If a long filename (254 chars) + a Unicode character that ends in 0x2E ('.') + an "extension" with "/" or "\" in it could change the final path.  Another potential method would be to use a unicode char that ends in byte "~" to point to the home dir on Linux.  I will see if I can update the python example.



<span class="line"><!---->I reviewed the code you pointed out, this could potentially allow an attacker to craft a "content-disposition" header that would save a file in a location other than the user intended. For example, it allows a 12 char "final extension". If a long filename (254 chars) + a Unicode character that ends in 0x2E ('.') + an "extension" with "/" or "\" in it could change the final path.  Another potential method would be to use a unicode char that ends in byte "~" to point to the home dir on Linux.  I will see if I can update the python example.<!----></span>

<br>





Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.

          position: relative;

          position: absolute;

          border: var(--chops-accessible-border);
          z-index: 999;

          border-spacing: 0;
          border-collapse: collapse;

           * height of the viewport, we want to make sure
           * there's spacing. */
          margin-bottom: 1em;

          display: block;
          min-width: 100px;
          max-height: 500px;
          overflow: auto;

         * is disabled for this component.
         */
        .chops-autocomplete-container {
          position: relative;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container table {
          padding: 0;
          font-size: var(--chops-main-font-size);
          color: var(--chops-link-color);
          position: absolute;
          background: var(--chops-white);
          border: var(--chops-accessible-border);
          z-index: 999;
          box-shadow: 2px 3px 8px 0px hsla(0, 0%, 0%, 0.3);
          border-spacing: 0;
          border-collapse: collapse;
          /* In the case when the autocomplete extends the
           * height of the viewport, we want to make sure
           * there's spacing. */
          margin-bottom: 1em;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tbody {
          display: block;
          min-width: 100px;
          max-height: 500px;
          overflow: auto;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr {
          cursor: pointer;
          transition: background 0.2s ease-in-out;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr[data-selected] {
          background: var(--chops-active-choice-bg);
          text-decoration: underline;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container td {
          padding: 0.25em 8px;
          white-space: nowrap;
        }
        .screenreader-hidden {
          clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);
          height: 1px;
          overflow: hidden;
          position: absolute;
          white-space: nowrap;
          width: 1px;
        }
      </style>
      <div class="chops-autocomplete-container">
        <span class="screenreader-hidden" aria-live="polite">
          
        </span>
        <table hidden="">
          <tbody>
            
          </tbody>
        </table>
      </div>
    <!----></mr-autocomplete>
            </div>
          </div>

      <style>
        mr-issue-page {
          --mr-issue-page-horizontal-padding: 12px;

        }

 runOnLoad(function() {
 if (typeof(ClientLogger) === "function") {
 let cl = new ClientLogger("issues");
 if (cl.started("new-issue")) {
 cl.logEnd("new-issue", null, 120 * 1000);
 }
 if (cl.started("issue-search")) {
 cl.logEnd("issue-search");
 }
 }
 });
